'pause':\n   230→      case 'resume':\n   231→        throw new ERR_HTTP2_NO_SOCKET_MANIPULATION();\n   232→      default: {\n   233→        const ref = stream.session !== undefined ?\n   234→ 'destroyed':\n   252→      case 'on':\n   253→      case 'once':\n   254→      case 'end':\n   255→      case 'emit':\n   256→      case 'destroy':\n   257→        stream[prop] = value;\n   258→ // If the user didn't interact with incoming data and didn't pipe it,\n   293→  // dump it for compatibility with http1\n   294→  if (!state.didRead && !req._readableState.resumeScheduled)\n   295→ 304→  return function onStreamTimeout() {\n   305→    const obj = this[kind];\n   306→    obj.emit('timeout');\n   307→  };\n   308→}\n   309→\n   310→class Http2ServerRequest extends Readable {\n   311→  constructor(stream, headers, options, rawHeaders) {\n   312→    super({ autoDestroy: false, ...options });\n   313→    this[kState] = {\n   314→      closed: false,\n   315→      didRead: assertValidHeader(name, value);\n   659→\n   660→    if (!isConnectionHeaderAllowed(name, value)) {\n   661→      return;\n   662→    }\n   663→\n   664→    if (name[0] === ':')\n   665→ value);\n   673→    }\n   674→\n   675→    if (!ArrayIsArray(headers[name])) {\n   676→      headers[name] = [headers[name]];\n   677→    }\n   678→\n   679→    const existingValues = headers[name];\n   680→    if (ArrayIsArray(value)) {\n   681→      for (let i = 0, length = value.length; i < length; i++) {\n   682→        existingValues.push(value[i]);\n   683→      }\n   684→    } else {\n   685→      existingValues.push(value);\n   686→    }\n   687→  }\n   688→\n   689→  get statusMessage() {\n   690→    statusMessageWarn();\n   691→\n   692→    return '';\n   693→  }\n   694→\n   695→ 707→\n   708→    if (state.closed || this.stream.destroyed || this.stream.closed)\n   709→      return this;\n   710→    if (this[kStream].headersSent)\n   711→      throw new To do so, we first remove any\n   724→        // existing conflicts, then use appendHeader. This is the\n   725→        // slow path, which only applies when you use setHeader and\n   726→        // then pass headers in writeHead too.\n   727→\n   728→        // We need to handle both the tuple and flat array formats, just\n   729→        // like the logic further below.\n   730→        if (headers.length && ArrayIsArray(headers[0])) {\n   731→          for (let n = 0; n < // Append all the headers provided in the array:\n   744→      if (headers.length && ArrayIsArray(headers[0])) {\n   745→        for (i = 0; i < headers.length; i++) {\n   746→          const header = headers[i];\n   747→          this[kAppendHeader](header[0], header[1]);\n   748→        }\n   749→      } else {\n   750→        if (headers.length % 2 !== 0) {\n   751→          throw new 756→        }\n   757→      }\n   758→    } else if (typeof headers === 'object') {\n   759→      const keys = ObjectKeys(headers);\n   760→      let key = '';\n   761→      for (i = 0; i < keys.length; i++) {\n   762→        key = keys[i];\n   763→        this[kSetHeader](key, headers[key]);\n   764→      }\n   765→    }\n   766→\n   767→    state.statusCode = statusCode;\n   768→ this[kStream].uncork();\n   779→  }\n   780→\n   781→  write(chunk, encoding, cb) {\n   782→    const state = this[kState];\n   783→\n   784→    if (typeof encoding === 'function') {\n   785→      cb = encoding;\n   786→      encoding = 'utf8';\n   787→    }\n   788→\n   789→    let err;\n   790→    if (state.ending) {\n   791→      err = new ERR_STREAM_WRITE_AFTER_END();\n   792→    } else if 812→    const stream = this[kStream];\n   813→    const state = this[kState];\n   814→\n   815→    if (typeof chunk === 'function') {\n   816→      cb = chunk;\n   817→      chunk = null;\n   818→ state.headRequest === stream.headRequest) {\n   825→      if (typeof cb === 'function') {\n   826→        process.nextTick(cb);\n   827→      }\n   828→      return this;\n   829→    }\n   830→\n   831→    if (chunk !== null && chunk !== undefined)\n   832→      this.write(chunk, encoding);\n   833→\n   834→    state.headRequest = stream.headRequest;\n   835→    state.ending = true;\n   836→\n   837→    if (typeof cb === 'function') {\n   838→      if (stream.writableEnded)\n   839→        this.once('finish', cb);\n   840→      else\n   841→        stream.once('finish', cb);\n   842→    }\n   843→\n   844→    if (!stream.headersSent)\n   845→      this.writeHead(this[kState].statusCode);\n   846→\n   847→    if (this[kState].closed || stream.destroyed)\n   848→   904→    return true;\n   905→  }\n   906→\n   907→  writeEarlyHints(hints) {\n   908→    validateObject(hints, 'hints');\n   909→\n   910→    const headers = { __proto__: null };\n   911→\n   912→ This pattern appears in critical modules including HTTP client/server (_http_client.js, _http_outgoing.js, _http_incoming.js), crypto (crypto.js), streams (stream.js), DNS (dns.js), and filesystem operations (fs.js). \\n\\nThe HTTP/2 compatibility layer (lib/internal/http2/compat.js) demonstrates additional protection mechanisms, specifically using `ObjectHasOwn` for safe property checks and `ObjectAssign` for safe object merging. This file explicitly documents why Object.create(null) is used for headers initialization to prevent prototype pollution, noting that HTTP/2 uses this pattern intentionally for security.\\n\\nSafe property checking via `ObjectHasOwn` (a primordial safe version of hasOwnProperty) is employed in critical module loading (lib/internal/modules/cjs/loader.js), command-line parsing (lib/internal/util/parse_args/parse_args.js), clustering (lib/cluster.js), and HTTP output (lib/_http_outgoing.js).\\n\\nThe codebase uses a multi-layered approach: (1) `__proto__: null` initialization prevents prototype chain exploitation, (2) `ObjectHasOwn` ensures only direct properties are checked, (3) `ObjectAssign` with null-prototype objects safely merges properties, and (4) `Object.keys` iteration avoids inherited properties.
